                  DIAGONAL CYCLES AND EULER SYSTEMS II:
                THE BIRCH AND SWINNERTON-DYER CONJECTURE
                      FOR HASSE-WEIL-ARTIN L-FUNCTIONS


                                    HENRI DARMON AND VICTOR ROTGER


        Abstract. This article establishes new cases of the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer conjecture in an-
        alytic rank 0, for elliptic curves over Q viewed over the fields cut out by certain self-dual Artin
        representations of dimension at most 4. When the associated L-function vanishes (to even order вүҘ 2)
        at its central point, two canonical classes in the corresponding Selmer group are constructed and
        shown to be linearly independent assuming the non-vanishing of a Garrett-Hida p-adic L-function at
        a point lying outside its range of classical interpolation. The key tool for both results is the study of
        certain p-adic families of global Galois cohomology classes arising from Gross-Kudla-Schoen diagonal
        cycles in a tower of triple products of modular curves.

  6. Application to the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer conjecture                                                        46

                                                  Introduction
  Let E be an elliptic curve over Q and let
                                % : GQ = Gal (QМ„/Q) вҲ’вҶ’ AutL (V% ) вүғ GLn (L)
be an Artin representation with coefficients in a finite extension L вҠӮ QМ„ вҠӮ C of Q, factoring though
the Galois group of a finite extension H/Q. The Hasse-Weil-Artin L-series L(E, %, s) of E twisted by
%, defined on the right half-plane Re(s) > 3/2 by an absolutely convergent Euler product of degree 2n,
is expected to admit an analytic continuation to the whole complex plane.
   Let E(H)% := HomGQ (V% , E(H) вҠ— L) denote the %-isotypical component of the Mordell-Weil group
E(H), and define the analytic and algebraic rank of the twist of E by % as
                        ran (E, %) = ords=1 L(E, %, s),             r(E, %) = dimL E(H)% .
A Galois-equivariant refinement of the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer conjecture predicts that
                                                            ?
(1)                                             ran (E, %) = r(E, %).
  The main object of this article is to study conjecture (1) when % = %1 вҠ— %2 , where
                                              %1 , %2 : GQ вҲ’вҶ’ GL2 (L)
are odd, irreducible two-dimensional Artin representations satisfying det(%1 ) = det(%2 )вҲ’1 . This last
condition implies that % has real traces, i.e., is isomorphic to its dual, or contragredient, representation.
   Thanks to the major advances achieved in the last two decades, the elliptic curve E and the Artin
representations %1 and %2 are known to be associated to cuspidal newforms
                            f вҲҲ S2 (Nf ),        g вҲҲ S1 (Ng , ПҮ),       h вҲҲ S1 (Nh , ПҮвҲ’1 )
                                                           1
2                                 HENRI DARMON AND VICTOR ROTGER


of weight 2, 1, 1, respectively. The nebentype character ПҮ = det(%1 ) of g is an odd Dirichlet character
whose conductor divides both Ng and Nh .
   The L-function L(E, %, s) can be identified with the triple-product convolution L(f, g, h, s), whose
analytic continuation and functional equation follow from the work of Garrett, Piatetski-Shapiro and
Rallis. In particular, the analytic rank ran (E, %) is defined unconditionally, suggesting that (1) might
repay closer scrutiny in this setting.
   It is assumed throughout this work that the level Nf of f is relatively prime to Ng Nh . This implies
(cf. [Pr, thm. 1.4]) that all the local signs in the functional equation of L(f, g, h, s) = L(E, %, s) are
+1, hence that the same is true for the global sign, implying that ran (E, %) is even. Subject to these
hypotheses, the main results of this article are Theorems A and B below. (Cf. Theorem 6.7 and
Theorem 6.13 for somewhat more general statements.)
Theorem A. If L(E, %, 1) 6= 0 then E(H)% = 0.
Theorem A has broad implications for the arithmetic of E over ring class fields of quadratic fields,
both imaginary and real. For any ring class character ПҲ of a quadratic field K (of conductor relatively
prime to Nf =: NE ), let H/K denote the ring class field cut out by it, and define
              E(H)ПҲ = {P вҲҲ E(H) вҠ— L such that P Пғ = ПҲ(Пғ)P for all Пғ вҲҲ Gal (H/K)}.
When K is a real quadratic field, assume further that the pair (E, K) satisfies the non-vanishing
hypothesis of Definition 6.8. This mild hypothesis is expected to always hold, and is satisfied, for
example, as soon as E has quadratic twists E 0 of both possible signs for which L(E 0 /K, 1) 6= 0.
Corollary A1. If L(E/K, ПҲ, 1) 6= 0 then E(H)ПҲ = 0.
When K is imaginary quadratic, theorems of this sort were already established by a variety of ap-
proaches (cf. [Ko89], [BD97, Th.B], [BD99, Thm.1.2.], [BD05, Cor.4] and [Ne3, Th.AвҖҷ], for example)
using Heegner points on modular or Shimura curves, combined with p-adic techniques and/or con-
gruences between modular forms. Their common feature is that they ultimately rely on KolyvaginвҖҷs
Euler system of CM points and on some variant (either classical, or p-adic) of the Gross-Zagier formula
[GZ86]. The approach followed in this article makes no use of CM points, which accounts for why it
extends unconditionally to more general settings, including the case where K is a real quadratic field.
   The intimate connection between Corollary A1 for K real quadratic and the theory of Stark-Heegner
points initiated in [Da] is suggested by the articles [BDD07] and [LRV13], which give a conditional proof
of Corollary A1 resting on the algebraicity of Stark-Heegner points, essentially by replacing CM points
with their conjectural real quadratic counterparts in the proof of [BD99, Thm.1.2]. Stark-Heegner
points are still poorly understood, but the hope that the structures developed in the proof of Corollary
A1 might shed light on their algebraicity was an important motivation for the present work.
   Specialising Theorem A to the case where the representation % = %1 вҠ— %2 is irreducible establishes
the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer conjecture in analytic rank zero, in scenarios lying beyond the scope of
both Heegner and Stark-Heegner points. For instance, in the case where the projective representations
attached to %1 and %2 cut out the same A5 -extension of Q, but where %1 and %2 are not twists of each
other, Theorem A leads to the following instance of the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer over quintic fields,
which is spelled out in Theorem 6.11.
Corollary A2. Let E be an elliptic curve over Q, let K be a non-totally real quintic field with Galois
group A5 , and assume that the discriminants of E and K are coprime. Then
                 ords=1 L(E/K, s) = ords=1 L(E/Q, s) вҮ’ rank E(K) = rank E(Q).

   The second main theorem of this article is concerned with the case where L(E, %, s) vanishes at
s = 1 (and hence to order at least 2). Note that %1 and %2 are both regular, i.e., there exists Пғ вҲҲ GQ
acting on each of these Galois representations with distinct eigenvalues.
   Fix an odd prime p not dividing N := lcm(Nf , Ng , Nh ) at which f is not Eisenstein and fix through-

of %g (Frobp ) and %h (Frobp ), respectively. It shall be assumed throughout this article that

   Theorem B below relates the p-Selmer group attached to E and % to the behaviour of the Garrett-
Hida p-adic L-functions attached to f , g, and h. In order to describe these p-adic L-functions more
precisely, let SОӣМғord (M, ПҲ) denote the space of ordinary Оӣ-adic modular forms of tame level M вүҘ 1 and

These spaces are locally free ОӣМғ-modules of finite rank, and are equipped with a natural ОӣМғ-linear action
of the Hecke operators.
   A Hida family ПҶ can be viewed concretely as a formal q-series with coefficients in ОӣМғ whose special-
isations give rise to a p-adically coherent collection {ПҶx } of overconvergent ordinary modular forms

of overconvergent modular forms of weight k, and is classical when k вүҘ 2 by [Hi93, Ch. 7.3, Thm. 3].
When k = 1, the form ПҶx may be classical or not.

   Let Selp (E, %) := Hfin (Q, Vp (E) вҠ— V% вҠ—L Lp ) denote the %-isotypic component of the Bloch-Kato
Selmer group of E/H; cf. (154) for the precise definition of this group. The following theorem shows
that the above p-adic values convey non-trivial information about Selp (E, %).
Theorem B. If L(E, %, 1) = 0 and Lp gОұ (fЛҳ, gМҶ вҲ— , hМҶ) 6= 0 for some choice of test vectors, then
                                                         dimLp Selp (E, %) вүҘ 2.
                                 DIAGONAL CYCLES AND EULER SYSTEMS II                                          5


  The same conclusion applies, of course, when any of the four p-adic L-values in (10) is non-zero.
Recent joint work with Alan Lauder [DLR] describes an algorithm for calculating the expressions in
(8), and hence Lp gОұ (fЛҳ, gМҶОұвҲ— , hМҶОұ ), and uses this to verify their non-vanishing in many instances of analytic
rank two, showing that Theorem B is not vacuous.
    Theorem D below formulates a more precise version of Theorem B, in which two canonical elements
in Selp (E, %) are associated to the data (f, gОұ , h), and shown to be linearly independent under the
hypotheses of Theorem B. One of the main contributions of [DLR] and [DR15] is the formulation of a
conjecture expressing these two elements as explicit p-adic linear combinations of global points in the
Mordell-Weil group attached to E(H)% . (Cf. loc.cit. for the precise statement of this conjecture and a
summary of the experimental evidence that has been gathered in its support.)
    Theorem B can be compared to the Theorem B of Skinner and Urban [SU], which asserts that the
rank of the Selmer group of an elliptic curve is вүҘ 2 when the associated L-function vanishes to even
order вүҘ 2. There is little overlap between both theorems, whose methods of proof are very different.
The result of [SU] has the virtue of requiring no non-vanishing hypotheses on an auxiliary p-adic L-
function, while Theorem B applies to a different class of Artin representations, typified by the settings
described in Corollaries A1 and A2.
    The proofs of Theorems A and B rest on a system of global cohomology classes for the Rankin
convolution of three modular forms of weights (2, 1, 1), whose construction is one of the main contri-
butions of the present work. These classes arise from generalised Gross-Kudla-Schoen cycles in the
product of three Kuga-Sato varieties fibered over a classical modular curve, and (crucially) from their
variation in Hida families.
    The prequel [DR13] to the present work initiated the authorsвҖҷ study of generalised Gross-Kudla-
Schoen cycles, relating their images under the p-adic Abel-Jacobi map to special values of Garrett-Hida
p-adic L-series attached to the triple convolution of three (Hida families of) cusp forms. The p-adic
Abel-Jacobi map has the featureвҖ”not present in its complex analogue, or in related complex and
p-adic heightsвҖ”of factoring through the restriction to GQp of its p-adic eМҒtale counterpart. This turns
out to be crucial in arithmetic applications relying on the theory of Euler systems. More precisely, the
eМҒtale Abel-Jacobi images of generalised diagonal cycles give rise, after applying suitable projections,
to distinguished global Galois cohomology classes
(11)                                 Оә(fx , gy , hz ) вҲҲ H 1 (Q, Vfx gy hz (N )),
where
      вҖў fx , gy and hz are classical specialisations of weights k, `, and m which are balanced in the sense
        that each weight is strictly smaller than the sum of the other two;
      вҖў Vfx gy hz (N ) is the Kummer self-dual twist of the direct sum of several copies of the tensor
        product of the p-adic representations Vfx , Vgy , Vhz of GQ attached by Eichler-Shimura and
        Deligne to these forms, occuring in the middle cohomology of a Kuga-Sato variety Ek (resp. E` ,
        Em ) of dimension k вҲ’ 1 (resp. ` вҲ’ 1, m вҲ’ 1).
The extensions of p-adic Galois representations associated to the classes Оә(fx , gy , hz ) arise from geom-
etry; namely, they are realised in the p-adic eМҒtale cohomology of an open subvariety of the product of
Kuga-Sato varieties Ek,`,m := Ek Г— E` Г— Em , which have good reduction at p. In particular, thanks to
the work of Saito their restrictions to a decomposition group at p are known to be crystalline.
   The main theorem of [DR13] can be interpreted as a direct relationship between the Bloch-Kato
p-adic logarithms of the class Оә(fx , gy , hz ) and the special values of Garrett-Hida p-adic L-functions
at points which lie outside their range of classical interpolation. The concluding paragraphs of the
introduction to [DR13] stressed the desirability of deforming this result along p-adic families and, in
particular, of p-adically interpolating the classes Оә(fx , gy , hz ) themselves as the triple (fx , gy , hz ) is
made to vary over the classical, balanced specialisations of ordinary Hida families f , g and h. Such a
p-adic interpolation would be described by a global cohomology class

homomorphisms
                                        ОҪxyz : Vf g h (N ) вҲ’вҶ’ Vfx gy hz (N ).
   The putative class Оә(f , g, h) would be uniquely determined by the requirement that its specialisations
at balanced triples (fx , gy , hz ) should agree, up to normalisation by elementary fudge factors, with the
classes Оә(fx , gy , hz ) of (11). Guided by this ideal goal but falling somewhat short of it, Chapter 1
attaches a one-variable cohomology class to a triple (f, g, h) formed by an eigenform f of weight two
and trivial nebentype and two Hida families g and h of tame character ПҮ and ПҮвҲ’1 , respectively. This
Оӣ-adic class is described by:
      вҖў a finite flat algebra Оӣf gh over the Iwasawa algebra Оӣ = Zp [[1 + pZp ]];
      вҖў a Оӣf gh [GQ ]-module Vf gh (N ) whose classical specialisations are of the form Vf gy hz (N ) where
        the pairs (gy , hz ) range over the specializations of g and h at classical points of the same weight
        ` and nebentype character at p;
      вҖў a cohomology class Оә(f, gh) вҲҲ H 1 (Q, Vf gh (N )).
The class Оә(f, gh) gives rise to a collection of global classes in H 1 (Q, Vf gy hz (N )), varying p-adic analyt-
ically as (gy , hz ) varies over pairs of specialisations of g and h with common weight and nebenytpe char-
acter at p. In order to construct Оә(f, gh), Section 1.3 introduces a family {вҲҶs }sвүҘ1 of null-homologous
twisted diagonal cycles on certain twists of finite quotients of the three-folds X0 (N p) Г— X1 (N ps ) Г—
X1 (N ps ), satisfying an explicit compatibility under the natural push-forward maps as s varies. The
class Оә(f, gh) is then manufactured in В§1.4-1.6 as the inverse limit of the cohomology classes one obtains
as the image of вҲҶs under a suitable projection of the p-adic eМҒtale Abel-Jacobi map.
   Although Оә(f, gh) is constructed by interpolating geometric constructions attached only to the
weight two specialisations of g and h, it makes sense to consider its specialisations
(13)                            Оә(f, gy , hz ) := Оә(f, gh)y,z вҲҲ H 1 (Q, Vf gy hz (N ))
at any point (y, z) attached to a pair (gy , hz ) of classical modular forms of arbitrary weight ` вүҘ 1
with inverse tame nebentype characters. The relevance of this class to the proof of Theorems B and
C arises when f is the weight 2 newform associated to the elliptic curve E, and gy = gОұ and hz = hОұ
are (ordinary) p-stabilisations of the forms g and h associated to the Artin representations %1 and %2 .
   Since gОұ 6= gОІ and hОұ 6= hОІ , the construction described above yields four relevant cohomology
classes, denoted
(14)         Оә(f, gОұ , hОұ ),   Оә(f, gОұ , hОІ ),   Оә(f, gОІ , hОұ ),   Оә(f, gОІ , hОІ )   вҲҲ H 1 (Q, Vf gh (N )),
where again Vf gh (N ) is just a direct sum of several copies of Vp (E) вҠ— V% вҠ—L Lp . These classes are
called the generalised Kato classes attached to the triple (f, g, h) of modular forms of weights (2, 1, 1).
Justifying this terminology is the fact that the classes of (14) were first constructed and studied by
Kato in the special case where both g and h are weight one Eisenstein series, where they form the
basis for his remarkable proof of the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer conjecture in analytic rank zero for
L-functions of elliptic curves twisted by Dirichlet characters.
   The Kummer-self-dual representation Vf gh is still crystalline, but there is no a priori reason for the
classes in (14) to be crystalline at p because the weights (2, 1, 1) of the triple (f, g, h) are unbalanced,
with f being the eigenform of dominant weight in the sense of [DR13] and thus the points in weight
space attached to the classes in (14) lie outside the range of вҖңgeometric interpolationвҖқ defining Оә(f, gh).
   Theorem 6.4 of В§5.2 establishes a reciprocity law relating the image of the classes in (14) under the
Bloch-Kato dual exponential map to the central critical value L(E, %, 1). It is the main ingredient in
the proof of Theorem A.
Theorem C. The generalised Kato class Оә(f, gОұ , hОұ ) is crystalline at p if and only if L(E, %, 1) = 0.
   When L(E, %, 1) 6= 0, Theorem C combined with the regularity of Vg and Vh at p implies that
the cohomology classes in (14) are linearly independent, more precisely, that their natural images
generate the вҖңsingular quotientвҖқ of the local cohomology at p. A standard argument involving the
global Poitou-Tate exact sequence then implies that the image of the Selmer group of Vf gh maps to
zero in the local cohomology H 1 (Qp , Vf gh ) at p. The fact that the Mordell-Weil group of global points
always injects into the group of local points then shows the triviality of the %-isotypical component of
the Mordell-Weil group of E, thereby proving Theorem A.
                                DIAGONAL CYCLES AND EULER SYSTEMS II                                         7


    One also expects (as a consequence of the Shafarevich-Tate conjecture) that Selp (E, %) is trivial when
E(H)%L is, but the proof of Theorem A described above does not yield the finiteness of the associated
Selmer group or Shafarevich-Tate group. The Gross-Schoen diagonal cycles can be viewed as a special
instance of a broader class of examples, namely the вҖңEuler systems of Garrett-Rankin-Selberg typeвҖқ
described in [BCDDPR], which also encompass KatoвҖҷs Euler system of Beilinson elements and the
Euler system of Beilinson-Flach elements. In both these settings, finiteness results for the Shafarevich-
Tate groups have been obtained by Kato [Ka98] and Lei, Loeffler, and Zerbes [LLZ1] respectively.
It would be of great interest to extend these authorsвҖҷ refinements to the setting of diagonal cycles.
Recent work of Yifeng Liu makes striking progress in a closely related setting, where diagonal cycles
are replaced by twisted variants on the product of a modular curve and a Hilbert modular surface
[Liu1] and on a Hilbert modular threefold [Liu2], and the Selmer groups that are studied are those
attached to Galois representations of weights (2, 2, 2) (in the region of вҖңbalanced weightsвҖқ, which can
thus be treated without recourse to the p-adic deformation of Abel-Jacobi images of cycles).
    When L(E, %, 1) = 0, and hence ran (E, %) вүҘ 2, Theorem C implies that the four classes in (14)
belong to the Selmer group Selp (E, %). The submodule of Selp (E, %) generated by these four classes
is expected to be non-trivial precisely when ran (E, %) = 2, i.e., when L00 (E, %, 1) 6= 0. The following
result, whose proof is described in Theorem 6.13 of Section 6.4, involves Lp gОұ (fЛҳ, gМҶ вҲ— , hМҶ) rather than
L00 (f, g, h, 1), and directly implies Theorem B above.

Theorem D. If L(E, %, 1) = 0 and Lp gОұ (fЛҳ, gМҶ вҲ— , hМҶ) 6= 0 for some choice of test vectors, there exist
GQ -equivariant projections jОұ , jОІ : Vf gh (N ) вҶ’ Vp (E) вҠ— V% such that the classes ОәОұОұ = jОұ (Оә(f, gОұ , hОұ ))
and ОәОұОІ = jОІ (Оә(f, gОұ , hОІ )) are linearly independent in Selp (E, %).

    The canonical nature of the elements in Selp (E, %) described in Theorem D is key to the formulation
of the conjectures of [DLR] and [DR15], which seem to admit no direct counterpart for the Selmer
classes constructed in [SU, Thm. B]. To further compare Theorem D with the results of [SU], note
that generalised Kato classes can only contribute to the pro-p Selmer group Selp (E/Q) of E over Q
when % contains the trivial representation as a constituent, which occurs precisely when g and h = gМ„
are dual to each other, so that % = 1 вҠ• Ad0 (%g ), where Ad0 (%g ) denotes the three dimensional adjoint
of %g , consisting of the trace zero endomorphisms of %g . In the scenario where L(E/Q, s) admits a
double zero at the center, the elliptic Stark conjectures of [DLR] predict that all of the p-adic L-values
in (10) vanish and that the generalised Kato classes attached to (f, g, gМ„) never generate the Selmer
group or Mordell-Weil group of E. However, they are expected to generate a one-dimensional subspace
of Selp (E/Q) whenever L(E, Ad0 (%g ), 1) 6= 0, consisting of the classes whose restriction to Qp lies in
the kernel of the logarithm map logp : E(Qp ) вҲ’вҶ’ Qp . The non-triviality of such a class only implies
that dim Selp (E/Q) вүҘ 1, but it does imply that rank(E(Q)) вүҘ 2 under the further (highly non-trivial)
assumption that LLI(E/Q) is finite. See [DR15, В§4.5] for a more detailed discussion of this intriguing
scenario.
    Underlying the crucial reciprocity law relating the local behaviour at p of the global classes in (14)
to p-adic L-values is a precise relationship between the p-adic families Оә(f, gh) of global cohomology
classes (more precisely, their restriction to a decomposition group at p) and the Garrett-Hida p-adic
L-functions alluded to above. See Theorem 5.3 for the precise statement. Such relationships are part
of a long tradition of explicit reciprocity laws going back to the seminal work of Coates and Wiles, and
even further to the work of Kummer, Iwasawa and Kubota-Leopoldt on the arithmetic of cyclotomic
fields. For more on how the approach of this paper fits into the larger perspective of Euler systems and
explicit reciprocity laws, notably with KatoвҖҷs work on Beilinson elements and the work of Bertolini
and the authors on Beilinson-Flach elements, the reader is invited to consult the survey [BCDDPR].

1.2. Modular curves. Let M вүҘ 1 be a positive integer and X0 (M ) and X1 (M ) denote the classical
modular curves over Q attached to the Hecke congruence subgroups О“0 (M ) and О“1 (M ), respectively.
   Several distinct models over Q of X1 (M ) occur in the literature; in what follows, the affine curve
Y1 (M ) obtained by removing the cusps from X1 (M ) is taken to be the coarse moduli space of pairs
(A, i) where A is an elliptic curve and i : ВөM вҶ’ A is an isomorphism between the group scheme ВөM
and a closed finite flat subgroup scheme of A. This model of X1 (M ) is characterized as being the
one whose field of rational functions Q(X1 (M )) is the subfield of C(X1 (M )) given by those functions
whose q-expansion at the cusp iвҲһ have rational coefficients.
   Fix an integer N вүҘ 3 and an odd prime p - N . For any s вүҘ 1, let Xs := X1 (N ps ). It will be
convenient to view Xs as classifying triples (A, iN , ip ) where iN : ВөN вҶ’ A and ip : Вөps вҶ’ A are
embeddings of finite group schemes. It will also be useful to consider the curve XsвҖ  /Q which arises as
the coarse moduli space associated to the problem of classifying triples (A, iN , P ) where (A, iN ) is as
above and P вҲҲ A is a point of exact order ps . The curves Xs and XsвҖ  are not naturally isomorphic over
Q, but are twists of each over the cyclotomic field of ps -th roots of unity. See below for more details.

   The next two sections explain how the ОӣМғ(N ) [GQ ]- module VordвҲһ realises one-parameter families of

give rise to p-adic families of Galois cohomology classes with values in these representations.

2.2.2. Weight one specializations. The richest arithmetic phenomena arise when studying the special-
isation of Оә(f, gh) at a point (y, z) of weight ` = 1 and trivial nebentype character at p, which will be
assumed in this section. The specializations of g and h at y and z need not be classical in general;
let us assume however that they are: the departure point of this section is the assumption that there
exist newforms g вҲҲ S1 (Ng , ПҮ) and h вҲҲ S1 (Nh , ПҮвҲ’1 ) such that
                                 gy = gОұ вҲҲ S1 (Ng p, ПҮ),       hz = hОұ вҲҲ S1 (Nh p, ПҮвҲ’1 ).
Recall from the introduction that associated to g and h there exist Artin representations %g and %h
with coefficients in a finite extension L/Q. Setting % = %g вҠ— %h , we have Vgh := Vg вҠ— Vh вүғ V% вҠ—L Lp .
   After labelling the two (distinct, by the hypothesis imposed in the introduction) roots of the p-th
Hecke polynomial x2 вҲ’ ap (g) + ПҮ(p) as Оұg and ОІg , one may define the global cohomology class
                                    Оә(f, gОұ , hОұ ) := Оә(f, gh)y,z вҲҲ H 1 (Q, Vf gh (N ))
with values in the Galois representation Vf gh (N ) = Vf (N p) вҠ— Vg (N p) вҠ— Vh (N p) вүғ (Vf вҠ— Vgh )a for
some a вүҘ 1. Let also Оәfp (f, gОұ , hОұ ) вҲҲ H 1 (Qp , Vffgh (N )) denote the associated local cohomology class
arising likewise from (75).
   The weight one setting distinguishes itself in (at least) two further respects. Firstly, recall the
running assumption that Оұg 6= ОІg , Оұh 6= ОІh . Let us denote g Оұ , g ОІ , hОұ , hОІ the Hida families passing
through gОұ , gОІ , hОұ , hОІ , respectively. One thus obtains four (a priori distinct) global classes

   Since Vgh is an Artin representation which is unramified at p, and for which both Vg and Vh are

           3. The syntomic Abel-Jacobi map on products of semistable curves
3.1. The cohomology of semistable curves. This section recalls the description (following [CI99],
and [CI10]) of the de Rham cohomology of a semistable curve and the attendant structures with which
it is equipped. Let F be a finite extension of Qp , let OF denote its ring of integers, fix an uniformizer
ПҖF and let kF = OF /ПҖF denote the residue field. Let F0 denote the maximal unramified subfield of F ,
which is isomorphic to the fraction field of the ring of Witt vectors of kF . Write Пғ0 вҲҲ Gal (F0 /Qp ) for
the Frobenius element generating the Galois group of F0 /Qp . Let X be a smooth, connected, proper
curve over F and assume it possesses a regular semistable model X over OF , meaning that locally at
every point, X is either smooth over Spec(OF ) or eМҒtale over Spec(OF [X, Y ]/(XY вҲ’ ПҖF )).
    Let XМғ denote the special fiber of X . It is assumed that the irreducible components of XМғ are smooth,
geometrically irreducible, and defined over kF , that there are at least two of them, and that distinct
components intersect only in ordinary double points defined over kF . Let G denote the dual graph of
the special fiber, whose set V(G) of vertices is in bijection with the irreducible components of XМғ and
whose set E(G) of oriented edges is in bijection with the singular points of the special fiber, together
with an ordering of the two components which intersect at that point. Given v вҲҲ V(G), let XМғv denote
the associated component, and let XМғvsm denote the smooth locus of XМғv , that is to say, the complement
in XМғv of the singular points of XМғ . If e вҲҲ E(G) is an edge of G, write s(e) and t(e) for its source and
target respectively, and xe for the associated ordinary double point, satisfying XМғs(e) вҲ© XМғt(e) = {xe }.
Write also eМ„ for the reversed edge, satisfying s(eМ„) = t(e) and t(eМ„) = s(e); note that xeМ„ = xe .
    Let

3.2. An analytic recipe for the syntomic Abel-Jacobi map. The goal of this section is to give
an analytic expression for the syntomic Abel-Jacobi map on the Chow group of codimension two cycles
on the triple product of semistable curves, in terms of ColemanвҖҷs theory of p-adic integration of rigid
differential forms. It will be convenient to place oneself in the abstract setting given by conditions (a)-
(d) below. While ostensibly somewhat special, this setting will nonetheless suffice for the applications
in this paper.
    (a) The ambient three-fold is a product W = X1 Г— X2 Г— X3 of three semistable curves over F .
For i = 1, 2, 3, write Gi for the dual graph of the special fiber of Xi , and let ОҰi = {ОҰi,v }vвҲҲV(Gi ) denote

4.1. The rigid geometry of modular curves. Let X1 (N ps ) be the proper, flat, regular model of
Xs over Zp [О¶s ] considered in [KM85, В§12]. Its special fiber is the union of a finite number of reduced
Igusa curves Igj over Fp , meeting (not always transversally) at their supersingular points. Among these
irreducible components there are two which are isomorphic to the Igusa curve Ig(N ps ) representing the
moduli problem (О“1 (N ), Ig(ps )) over Fp specified in [KM85, В§12]. These are called the good components,
and are labelled IgвҲһ and Ig0 . More precisely, IgвҲһ classifies ordinary elliptic curves with О“1 (N )-level
structure and a chosen section of order ps in its canonical subgroup of order ps .
   Let F/Qp (О¶s ) be a finite extension over which Xs acquires semistable reduction, with valuation ring
OF and residue field kF . Let ПҖ : Xs вҶ’ X1 (N ps ) Г— OF be a semistable model of Xs over OF , obtained
by applying sufficiently many blow-ups to the base change of X1 (N ps ) to OF . The map ПҖ is birational
and induces an isomorphism between the generic fibers and also between two of the components of
the closed fibre of Xs with IgвҲһ Г— kF and Ig0 Г— kF , respectively. By an abuse of notation, continue to
denote IgвҲһ and Ig0 the two components of the closed fibre of Xs corresponding to the two latter. Let
                                                    red : Xs (F ) вҲ’вҶ’ XМғs (kF )
denote the вҖңmod pвҖқ reduction map. The inverse images of the irreducible components of the special
fiber of Xs give a finite collection of wide open subsets of Xs (F ) which form an admissible cover of
this rigid analytic space, as in the discussion in В§3.1. Let W O(Xs ) denote the collection of wide open
spaces in this admissible cover.
   Denote by WвҲһ (ps ) and W0 (ps ) the wide open spaces in W O(Xs ) arising as the inverse image of
IgвҲһ and Ig0 , respectively, under the reduction map. The inverse image of the smooth locus of IgвҲһ ,
denoted AвҲһ (ps ), is the underlying affinoid of WвҲһ (ps ) and an analogous definition is made for A0 (ps ).
   The F -valued points of the rigid analytic space AвҲһ (ps ) are in bijection with triples (A, iN , ip ) where
A is an ordinary (generalised) elliptic curve over OF , iN : ВөN вҲ’вҶ’ A[N ] is an injective map of group

5.2. The triple product p-adic L-functions via Оӣ-adic cohomology classes. We are now in

regulator maps. Realising a p-adic L-function in this way has strong arithmetic consequences, some of
which shall be explored in the remainder of this article.

                6. Application to the Birch and Swinnerton-Dyer conjecture
     As in the introduction, let

   Turning to Corollary A1 of the introduction, let K be a quadratic field of discriminant prime to
the conductor NE of E. If ПҲ is a finite order ray class character of K, let ПҲ 0 denote the character
obtained from it by composing with the automorphism of K/Q. A ring class character is a character
of K with trivial central character, which therefore satisfies ПҲ 0 = ПҲ вҲ’1 . Let О K denote the set of all
ring class characters of conductor prime to NE . When K is a real quadratic field, the set О K can be
                                       вҲ’
partitioned into two subsets О +
                              K and О K , consisting of totally even and totally odd ring class characters,
                                      вҲ’                                         вҲ’
respectively. Let О E/K , О E/K and О E/K denote the subsets of О K , О +
                           +
                                                                       K and О K respectively consisting
of the characters for which L(E/K, ПҲ, 1) 6= 0.
   To the pair (E, K) one can associate the sign sgn(E, K) вҲҲ {Вұ1} of the functional equation for
the L-function L(E/K, s). It turns out that this is the very same sign that occurs in the functional
equation of L(E/K, ПҲ, s) for any ПҲ вҲҲ О K . In particular, О E/K is empty when sgn(E, K) = вҲ’1.
   When sgn(E, K) = 1 and K is imaginary quadratic, a non-vanishing theorem of Cornut and Vatsal
shows that О E/K is infinite. If K is real quadratic, a simple argument involving congruences for
                                                                              вҲ’
L-values shows that О +  E/K is either empty or infinite, and likewise for О E/K . The scenario where
  Вұ
О E/K = вҲ… is highly unlikely, since it would provide us with a systematic supply of ring class characters
for which the (primitive) L-function L(E/K, ПҲ, s) admits at least a double zero at the center.

Definition 6.8. The pair (E, K) is said to satisfy the non-vanishing hypothesis if О +
                                                                                    E/K and О E/K
are both non-empty (and hence, infinite).
   When K is real, a proof of this non-vanishing hypothesis does not seem out of reach of current
techniques in analytic number theory, although the unavailability of an вҖңanti-cyclotomic Zp -extensionвҖқ
of K prevents a straightforward application of the methods of Cornut and Vatsal.
Lemma 6.9. For all ПҲ вҲҲ О K , there exists a ray class character ПҲ0 of K of conductor prime to NE
such that ПҲ = ПҲ0 /ПҲ00 .
Proof. Let M/K be the cyclic extension of K (of degree n, say) which is cut out by the character ПҲ.
This field is Galois over Q, and Gal (M/Q) is isomorphic to the dihedral group Dn of order 2n, furnished
with a natural embedding into the semi-direct product (CГ— oZ/2Z) via the characterПҲ. Embed Dn into
PGL2 (C) by sending О» вҲҲ CГ— to the class of any diagonal matrix of the form О»01 О»02 , where О»1 /О»2 = О»
                                                                              
modulo the center, and sending some reflection in Dn to the matrix 01 10 . This yields a projective
representation rМ„ : GQ вҶ’ PGL2 (C). By a classical result of Tate on the vanishing of H 2 (Q, Q/Z(1)), the
projective representation rМ„ may be lifted to a linear representation r : GQ вҶ’ GL2 (C). By construction,
the representation r has dihedral projective image, and hence is induced from some character ПҲ0 of K.
The restriction of r to GK is then equal to the direct sum ПҲ0 вҠ• ПҲ00 . It follows that the restriction of rМ„
to GK is identified with ПҲ0 /ПҲ00 , and therefore that ПҲ0 /ПҲ00 = ПҲ. To show that ПҲ0 can be chosen to be
unramified at the primes of K dividing NE , observe that for each prime `|NE , the linear representation
r maps the inertia group at ` to the subgroup CГ— of scalar matrices, since rМ„ is unramified at `. Now
choose a Dirichlet character ПҮ : GQ вҲ’вҶ’ CГ— whose restriction to I` agrees with the restriction of r,
for all `|NE , and replace r by r вҠ— ПҮвҲ’1 . This substitution does not affect the projective representation
attached to r, but leads to a representation r which is unramified at the primes dividing NE ; hence
the same is true for the resulting character ПҲ0 .                                                       

   Note that, if K is a real quadratic field, the character ПҲ0 is of mixed signature (resp. totally even
or odd) when ПҲ is totally odd (resp. totally even).
   By considering the case where Оұ is further restricted to be a quadratic character of K, it is clear
that the non-vanishing hypothesis is satisfied if there are two quadratic Dirichlet characters ПҮ (of the
two possible signatures) for which
(157)                          L(E, ПҮ, 1) 6= 0,   and    L(E, ПҮПҮK , 1) 6= 0,
where ПҮK is the (fixed) Dirichlet character attached to K. Such simultaneous non-vanishing results for
pairs of quadratic Dirichlet characters with fixed product seem to lie just beyond the reach of currently
available techniques. However, a character ПҮ satisfying (157) is widely expected to exist, and a quick
inspection is usually enough to produce such aвҲҡПҮ, for any given E and K. For example, if E is the elliptic
curve of smallest conductor 11 and K = Q( 5) is the real quadratic field of smallest discriminant 5,
a cursory inspection of the tables of Cremona reveals that L(E, ПҮ, 1) 6= 0 and L(E, ПҮПҮK , 1) 6= 0 when
     (1) ПҮ is the trivial character;
     (2) ПҮ is the odd quadratic character of conductor 4.
Hence the pair (E, K) satisfies the non-vanishing hypothesis.
Theorem 6.10. Let E be an elliptic curve over Q and let K be a quadratic field for which sign(E, K) =
1. When K is real, assume that (E, K) satisfies the non-vanishing hypothesis. Then for all ring class
characters ПҲ вҲҲ О K ,
                              L(E/K, ПҲ, 1) 6= 0 вҮ’ E(H)ПҲ = 0.
Proof. If ПҲ is a quadratic (genus) character, the statement already follows from the approach of Gross-
Zagier and Kolyvagin (or Kato), since the induced representation VПҲ decomposes as a sum of two
quadratic Dirichlet characters.
   Assume henceforth that ПҲ 2 6= 1, which amounts to saying that VПҲ is irreducible. Choose a character
Оұ вҲҲ О E/K which differs from ПҲ and ПҲ вҲ’1 , and for which VПҲ вҠ• VОұ is regular. If K is real, assume Оұ
to be of opposite signature to ПҲ. This choice is possible thanks to the non-vanishing hypothesis, and
implies that complex conjugation acts on VПҲ вҠ• VОұ with eigenvalues (1, 1, вҲ’1, вҲ’1).
                              DIAGONAL CYCLES AND EULER SYSTEMS II                                    51


   Invoking Lemma 6.9, let ПҲ0 and Оұ0 be ray class characters of K of conductors prime to NE and
satisfying ПҲ0 /ПҲ00 = ПҲ and Оұ0 /Оұ00 = Оұ, and set
                                   ПҲg := ПҲ0 Оұ0 ,     ПҲh := (ПҲ00 Оұ0 )вҲ’1 .
The two-dimensional representations
                                   %g := IndQ
                                            K ПҲg ,     %h := IndQ
                                                                K ПҲh

satisfy the following properties:
      вҖў det(%g ) = det(%h )вҲ’1 , because the central characters of ПҲg and ПҲh are inverses of each other,
      вҖў %g and %h are odd: this is automatic when K is imaginary; when K is real this follows because
         ПҲ and Оұ have opposite signature, hence exactly one of ПҲ0 and Оұ0 is of mixed signature, implying
         that both ПҲg and ПҲh are of mixed signature.
      вҖў %g and %h are irreducible: this amounts to saying that ПҲg 6= ПҲg0 and ПҲh 6= ПҲh0 ; tracing the
         definitions, this holds because Оұ has been chosen to be different from ПҲ and ПҲ вҲ’1 ;
      вҖў the conductors of %g and %h are prime to NE , and hence the same is true for the levels of the
         associated weight one modular forms.
The tensor product %gh decomposes as
(158)                       Vgh = VПҲg вҠ— VПҲh = VПҲg ПҲh вҠ• VПҲg ПҲh0 = VПҲ вҠ• VОұ .
Thorem 6.10 now follows from the regularity of Vg and Vh and from Theorem 6.7, since
               L(E, Vgh , 1) = L(E, VПҲ , 1)L(E, VОұ , 1) = L(E/K, ПҲ, 1)L(E/K, Оұ, 1) 6= 0.

  We now turn to the proof of Corollary A2 of the introduction:
Theorem 6.11. Let E be an elliptic curve over Q and let K be a non-real quintic extension of Q with
Galois group A5 , of discriminant prime to the conductor of E. Then
              ords=1 L(E/K, s) = ords=1 L(E/Q, s)       вҮ’     rank(E(K)) = rank(E(Q)).
Proof. Let KМғ denote the Galois closure of K and fix an embedding of the group A5 into PGL2 (C).
There are exactly two conjugacy classes of such embeddings, and the further choice of an isomorphism
Gal (KМғ/Q) = A5 gives rise to a projective representation
                               %М„g : GQ  Gal (KМғ/Q) вүғ A5 вҠӮ PGL2 (C).
TateвҖҷs lifting theorem produces a linear lift %g : GQ вҲ’вҶ’ GL2 (C) of %М„g , which is odd since K is not
totally real. An argument similar to the one concluding the proof of Lemma 6.9 also shows that %g
can be chosen to unramified at the primes dividing NE .
   Assume that the field H cut out by %g is a cyclic extension of KМғ of degree a power of 2. The
image of Gal (H/KМғ) under %g consists of scalar matrices whose diagonal entries are 2-power roots of
unity. Let Пғ be an automorphism
                     вҲҡ        вҲҡ     of C which agrees with complex conjugation on the 2-power roots
of unity and sends 5 to вҲ’ 5, and let %h be the Artin representation obtained by applying Пғ to
the matrix entries of %g . The tensor product %gh is a four-dimensional representation which factors
through Gal (KМғ/Q) = A5 since it is trivial on Gal (H/KМғ). To identify this representation, observe
that there are precisely two distinct irreducible two-dimensional representations,
                                                                       вҲҡ           denoted %1 and %2 ,
of the non-trivial central extension AМғ5 of A5 , whose traces lie in Q( 5) and which are conjugate to
each other over this field. Viewing %1 вҠ— %2 as a representation of Gal (KМғ/Q), one has
                                     %gh = %1 вҠ— %2 = (IndQ
                                                         K 1) вҲ’ 1,

where the last equality of virtual representations can be seen, for instance, by consulting the Atlas of
finite simple groups. The Artin formalism implies that
              ran (E, %gh ) = ran (E/K) вҲ’ ran (E/Q),       r(E, %gh ) = r(E/K) вҲ’ r(E/Q).
By hypothesis, ran (E, %gh ) = 0. Theorem 6.7 can now be invoked to conclude that r(E, %gh ) = 0, i.e.,
r(E, K) = r(E, Q). Theorem 6.11 follows.                                                             

6.4. Proof of Theorems B and D. We conclude with the proof of Theorem D of the introduction,
which in turn implies Theorem B. Assume for this section that
     (i) L(E, %gh , 1) = 0;
    (ii) the Artin representations %g and %h are both regular at p.

after (76), the global cohomology classes

that Оә(f, gОұ , hОұ ) and Оә(f, gОұ , hОІ ) belong to the Selmer group Selp (E, Vgh (N )), which can be identified
with a finite sum of copies of the Selmer group Selp (E, %gh ).
